Update (6/5/2017): - Several have reached out to me who have been through this same situation. I can't stress how immoral of a practice this is. Most people have recently had a new born and are already stressed enough dealing with that. To get a random bill for $3,000-$10,000 thousand dollars at a time when the stress and sleep deprivation in their life is already sky high is the worst. On top of that you have to spend several valuable hours on the phone dealing with it with billing. Shame on Natera.< /Text>

3) When I transferred out of this location, they refused to transfer the treatment files to the new orthodontist, causing them to have to start from scratch.

Good luck with your dentist/orthodontist selection... my advice is, if you read one bad review, trust me that means there are more, they just didn't take the time to report it.  How bad is it really?  This one is as bad as it can get.<//review>

This used to be my favorite restaurant in Sacramento, period.  I haven't been for a while and decided to order in.  What I got was a major disappointment.  The broth was flavorless, and barely enough to cover the noodles. The egg was hard boiled and unseasoned.  When I called to ask why it was different than I remembered, I was interrupted repeatedly by the person on the other end of the phone.
I even asked if they were under new ownership, it tasted so different. If I had been sitting in the restaurant and served what I had tonight, I would have sent it back and left.

Based on the interaction with the person on the phone and the lack of flavor in the food, I won't be back.< /Review>

I think this place is really hyped up. It definitely drew me to want to come in because of the fact that they make their broth from scratch sans MSG & preservatives!

Unfortunately the ramen did not blow our minds with amazing-ness. My bf and I admitted that we've definitely had better. My spicy tonkotsu didn't have a ton of flavor, it was a tad on the bland/mild tasting side.

I would rate this place a 3 star, but the customer service is amazing and I added an extra star just for that.

I don't think we will be returning here, but we did enjoy the overall experience here.< /Text>

<userid>103056484927859251458< /userid><user_name>Keith Davis</user_name><Time>1579239513423< /Time><rate>4< /rate><Review>Shoki Ramen, one of the original Ramen houses in Sacramento, is a local institution. While they may have changed locations, sizes, and prices over the years, the overly quality and delicious nature of the soup has remained a constant.

There are plenty of other places to get ramen in Sacramento but why look further when this classic is still serving up tasty noodles and soup in their convenient downtown location?

There can be a wait almost any time of year as it is very popular, so be prepared for that. I visited in January and there was approximately 20+ minutes wait to get a seat just for 2.

Typical price is about $9.90 for your choice of many different ramen dishes, and sides/appetizers run from $3-4 to $6-7 depending. They even have a small poke bowl for under $7!

Check it out for yourself and see what all the fuss is about, you won't be sad that you did üôÇ</Review><pics>None</pics>< response>

Stephanie Moris< /user_name>
<Review>Shoki has always been my favorite place for ramen in the Sacramento area. I've been coming to Shoki for many years and all throughout their numerous menu changes. While I can't say I've liked all the experiments they've done with the menu, I can say I've always enjoyed the broth of my go-to order: Kurogoma Tantan Men.

I typically order the Kurogoma Tantan Men (contains minced beef), but on my most recent visit I decided to try their newly added Vegetarian version of the item (Yasai Kurogoma Tantan Men).  I very much enjoyed this one as well!  Now I have something for when I feel like meat and something for when I want to go with veggies only. While the Kurogoma broth is not for everyone, I love the flavor of the black sesame seeds. They have many choices of ramen flavors, so if that doesn't sound appealing to you, give something else a try: shio (sea salt base), shoyu (soy sauce base), or curry (soy sauce base with curry sauce).

I know people who are partial to the less healthy ramen places, but I personally prefer the taste of the broth here compared to the numerous other ramen places that use MSG and unhealthy additives. I have always been in full support of the Owner's/Chef's passion for creating a healthier bowl of ramen, made from scratch and natural ingredients.

Even though they ignored my job application right when I graduated from high school, and I am reminded of that rejection every time I eat here to this very day, I return in spite of this because the ramen here is the best!< /Review><Response>None</Response>< Pics>
None<//Pics>

Location is small, food is great and the staff is very friendly and helpful with any questions you have or recommendations you may be looking for. The menu was easy to navigate and our group was served fairly quickly. The food was really good and unfortunately I forgot to take a picture as I was too busy devouring it. < review>
We did not need to wait on a Saturday at 5:30pm, however it did start to get quite busy soonafter. The wait staff are friendly and attentive, which contributed to an additional star in my review. We ordered the Shio ramen and Kurogoma tantanmen, but I had only personally tried the Shio ramen, which I do not recommend. The dashi/broth tastes predominantly of katsuobushi (bonito) and really nothing much else; it is a light and very bland broth. Ironically there is not enough salt in the Shio (salt) ramen. The noodles are average, with a slightly more stiff chew. The boiled cabbage, which is unflavored, included a piece of the core which was unfortunate. I was disappointed that the egg is not the typical ramen egg with a golden runny yolk. This is a plain old boiled egg, which is cooked well but would be more suited for deviled eggs. The raw acrid spinach on top does not work well with ramen.  My significant other who had the kurogoma ramen commented that the minced beef topping was refrigerator cold. Their ramen fares significantly below average.</review>

<Rate>2<//Rate><Text>Shoki was my favorite ramen joint in Sacramento. That being said, the quality here has continually declined each year. At first I was happy to see all the new options on the menu for vegetarians, vegans, gluten intolerant, etc, but it seems that each time the menu is stretched wider, the quality goes lower and lower. Even the basics weren't done correctly (I don't remember ordering my noodles al dente to the point that the cross section is half uncooked). A marinated egg should be complimentary with a bowl of ramen, but even after paying extra for it, it was tough (old) and didn't have any flavor. Similar also to the cha shu which was thinly cut, dry, and had no flavor. The details weren't cared about as can be seen by cold meat on the tan tan men and the undercooked noodles. Also the service was quite bad. The restaurant was not even half full and there was a wait just to get a menu. If I wait to be seated then the menu should come quite quickly. Furthermore if I have ramen then I shouldn't need to ask for the condiments. Then after asking for them they didn't bring the chili oil which was why I asked in the first place.

Shoki used to be the best, back when they had fewer menu items all cooked perfectly but those days have ended it seems. I will miss you Shoki.</Text><Pics>None<//Pics>< Resp>

<Text>First off, I don't recommend coming here at night since the location is pretty sketchy.

This is a tiny ramen stand and once you're inside it's like a diner/ramen bar atmosphere.

The bathroom is accessible via outside and through a key, maybe telling more about the sketchiness of the area.

I thought the ramen was just okay. I ordered a tonkotsu and it wasn't very flavorful. I ordered corn and they bowl was literally half corn. So I guess the ramen is pretty much however you choose to customize it. But the tonkotsu broth lacked a lot of flavor and my pork portions were small and not very good.

Maybe I'll try the soy milk or something special if I decide to come here again.< /Text>< Pictures>

<Date>1376066710203< /Date><user>101273326613955374435< /user>< review>
This is by far the best ramen place in Sacramento.  In fact, I'm confident enough to say that it's one of the top 5 ramen stores in all of California.  I've been to most of the best ramen stores in Los Angeles, the Peninsula, and San Francisco.  A few important tips.  Always get their tamago (boiled egg) with your ramen.  They cook it to perfection, and it has this delicate soy sauce flavor infused in them that makes them delicious and the star of the ramen bowl.  Their broth is deep, complex, but not overwhelmingly heavy.  It's actually pretty light.  Everything about their ramen bowl shows these guys really know what they're doing.  I would even go to this place if it was in Japan!  If you go there in the summer, also try their tomato ramen!</review>
